 Analyzing FlyingObject.vue requirements. This is a primitive animated component that:

  Thought 4/12 

 Analyzing FlyingPostFromIcon.vue orchestrator. This component composes the primitives:
- 1x AnimatedIcon.vue at a corner position (source)
- 2x FlyingObject.vue (2 posts per platform flying from icon to center)
- Receives: platform (icon name), corner ('top-left' | 'top-right' | 'bottom-left' | 'bottom-right'), iconSize, iconOffset, cardSize, targetX/Y (center position), posts (array of 2 post data), active
- Calculates start position based on corner prop
- Passes correct start/target positions to FlyingObjects
- Staggers the 2 posts with delay offset
- This is the orchestrator pattern - no UI of its own, just composition

  Thought 5/12 

 Analyzing UnifiedPostsStage.vue integration. The Stage will:
- Use 4x FlyingPostFromIcon.vue instances, one per corner
- Each instance gets: platform (fb/ig/tw/li), corner position, scaled dimensions from responsive plugin, target center coordinates
- Also composes UnifiedGrid.vue for the center 2x2 grid
- Uses single useAnimation with responsive plugin for all dimension scaling
- Passes scaled values as props to all children
- Children are position-absolute, Stage is position-relative container

Props flow: Stage (scaled dimensions)  FlyingPostFromIcon (position + dimensions)  AnimatedIcon + FlyingObject (final rendered props)

  Thought 6/12 

 Vue composition best practices for this architecture:
1. **Primitive > Orchestrator pattern** - AnimatedIcon and FlyingObject are primitives (dumb, highly reusable), FlyingPostFromIcon is orchestrator (smart, composes primitives)
2. **Props drilling is OK for 2-3 levels** - Stage  FlyingPostFromIcon  Primitives is acceptable
3. **Single source of scaling** - Only Stage has useAnimation responsive plugin, all children receive scaled values
4. **Slot composition** - FlyingObject uses default slot for flexibility
5. **Type safety** - All props typed with TypeScript interfaces
6. **SSR safe** - No browser APIs needed in these components
7. **Accessibility** - Icons need aria-label on AnimatedIcon

 Component interface design for AnimatedIcon.vue:
```typescript
interface Props {
  icon: string          // Iconify icon name (e.g., 'mdi:facebook')
  size: number          // Scaled pixel size
  chipPadding: number   // Scaled padding around icon
  active: boolean       // Controls pulse animation
  pulseSpeed?: number   // Animation duration in ms (default 2000)
  ariaLabel?: string    // Accessibility label
}
```

Template structure:
- Outer div with circular chip styling (glass effect?)
- Icon component from @iconify/vue
- CSS animation class bound to active prop
- No positioning (parent controls via absolute positioning)

  Thought 8/12 

 Component interface design for FlyingObject.vue:
```typescript
interface Props {
  startX: number        // Starting X position (px)
  startY: number        // Starting Y position (px)
  targetX: number       // Target X position (px)
  targetY: number       // Target Y position (px)
  width: number         // Object width (px)
  height: number        // Object height (px)
  delay?: number        // Animation delay (ms)
  duration?: number     // Animation duration (ms, default 800)
  active: boolean       // Controls animation play state
}
```

Implementation approach:
- Use CSS variables for start/target positions (--start-x, --start-y, --target-x, --target-y)
- CSS keyframe animation for the flight path (opacity + transform)
- Absolute positioning with initial transform from start position
- Default slot for flexible content (post card, icon, anything)
- animation-play-state bound to active prop

  Thought 9/12 

 Component interface design for FlyingPostFromIcon.vue (orchestrator):
```typescript
interface Platform {
  id: string           // 'facebook', 'instagram', etc.
  icon: string         // Iconify icon name
  color: string        // Brand color
  posts: PostData[]    // Array of 2 posts for this platform
}

interface Props {
  platform: Platform
  corner: 'top-left' | 'top-right' | 'bottom-left' | 'bottom-right'
  iconSize: number
  iconOffset: number
  chipPadding: number
  cardWidth: number
  cardHeight: number
  cardPadding: number
  centerX: number      // Target X (center of stage)
  centerY: number      // Target Y (center of stage)
  active: boolean
  staggerDelay?: number  // Delay between 2 posts (default 250ms)
}
```

Computed logic needed:
- Calculate icon start position based on corner + iconOffset
- Pass to AnimatedIcon and as startX/Y for FlyingObjects
- Posts get staggered: first at delay 0, second at staggerDelay

 UnifiedPostsStage.vue integration with new component structure:
```typescript
<template>
  <div ref="stageRef" class="unified-posts-stage">
    <!-- 4 Corner Platform Groups -->
    <FlyingPostFromIcon
      :platform="platforms.facebook"
      corner="top-left"
      :icon-size="scaled.platformIconSize"
      :icon-offset="scaled.iconOffset"
      :chip-padding="scaled.platformChipPadding"
      :card-width="scaled.flyingCardWidth"
      :card-height="scaled.flyingCardHeight"
      :card-padding="scaled.flyingCardPadding"
      :center-x="centerX"
      :center-y="centerY"
      :active="effectiveActive"
    />
    <!-- Repeat for top-right, bottom-left, bottom-right -->
    
    <!-- Center Grid -->
    <UnifiedGrid
      :posts="unifiedPosts"
      :card-width="scaled.centerCardWidth"
      :grid-gap="scaled.gridGap"
      :active="effectiveActive"
    />
  </div>
</template>
```

The Stage just composes the orchestrators, passing scaled dimensions. Clean separation of concerns.

  Thought 11/12 

 Key design decisions summary:
1. **Primitive Components** - AnimatedIcon.vue and FlyingObject.vue are highly reusable, have no business logic, just receive props and render
2. **Orchestrator Component** - FlyingPostFromIcon.vue composes 1 icon + 2 flying posts, calculates positions, manages one corner's behavior
3. **Stage as Composition Layer** - UnifiedPostsStage.vue uses responsive plugin for scaling, composes 4 FlyingPostFromIcon + 1 UnifiedGrid
4. **Props Flow** - Stage (useAnimation responsive)  FlyingPostFromIcon (position logic)  Primitives (pure rendering)
5. **No prop drilling issues** - Only 2-3 levels deep, all props are necessary at each level
6. **Reusability Win** - AnimatedIcon can be used anywhere for pulsing icons, FlyingObject can animate any content along any path
7. **Type Safety** - Full TypeScript interfaces for all props
8. **Accessibility** - aria-label on AnimatedIcon for screen readers

[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 1/8 

 Analyzing the layout problem: The current approach uses absolute positioning with manual calculations for each corner (top/left/right/bottom). This is error-prone because:
1. We have to manually calculate positions for right/bottom corners from stage dimensions
2. Flying objects need to know exact start positions
3. Small calculation errors compound across responsive scaling
4. Difficult to debug when positions don't align

The user's suggestion of using CSS Grid (33) is actually BRILLIANT because:
- Grid automatically handles positioning
- Icons naturally sit in corners
- Center grid is perfectly centered
- Responsive behavior is automatic
- No manual position calculations needed
- Much cleaner architecture

[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 2/8 

 Grid layout structure:
```css
display: grid;
grid-template-columns: auto 1fr auto;
grid-template-rows: auto 1fr auto;
```

Cell mapping:
- (1,1): Icon top-left
- (1,2): Empty (spacer)
- (1,3): Icon top-right
- (2,1): Empty (spacer)
- (2,2): UnifiedGrid (center)
- (2,3): Empty (spacer)
- (3,1): Icon bottom-left
- (3,2): Empty (spacer)
- (3,3): Icon bottom-right

Benefits:
- Auto-centering with `place-items: center`
- Icons naturally spaced from edges
- No manual offset calculations
- Responsive automatically adjusts spacing
- Clean CSS, no JavaScript positioning

[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 3/8 

 Flying objects positioning with grid:
Problem: Flying objects need to start FROM the icon center and fly TO the grid center.

With grid, each icon cell knows its own position via `getBoundingClientRect()`. But we want to avoid JavaScript for positioning if possible.

Alternative: Use CSS Grid positioning + CSS variables for flight animations:
- Icons still use grid cells (no change)
- Flying objects can use `position: absolute` with `inset: 0` to span entire stage
- Calculate start position based on which corner (using CSS calc or grid-area)
- Or: Flying objects as children of icon cells, use `position: absolute` to escape and fly

Actually, simplest approach:
- Stage uses CSS Grid for layout
- Icons placed in grid cells (natural positioning)
- Flying objects remain position: absolute with calculated positions
- BUT: We can use grid cell positions to get icon centers via JavaScript (getBoundingClientRect)
- Pass those positions as props to FlyingObject components

  Thought 4/8 

 Revised architecture with CSS Grid:

**Stage Component (UnifiedPostsStage.vue):**
- Use CSS Grid: 33 layout
- Grid cells auto-position icons and center grid
- No manual position calculations needed

**Icon positioning:**
- Grid cell (1,1): top-left icon
- Grid cell (1,3): top-right icon  
- Grid cell (3,1): bottom-left icon
- Grid cell (3,3): bottom-right icon
- Grid cell (2,2): UnifiedGrid (center)

**Flying objects:**
- Still need absolute positioning (to fly over grid)
- But we can use template refs to get actual icon positions after mount
- Use `getBoundingClientRect()` to get real icon centers
- Pass those real positions to FlyingObject components

This hybrid approach:
 Grid handles layout (clean, automatic)
 JavaScript gets actual positions for animations (accurate)
 No manual corner calculations
 Responsive works automatically

  Thought 5/8 

 Simplified implementation plan:

**Option 1: Pure Grid (Simpler)**
- Stage uses CSS Grid 33
- Icons placed in corner cells with `grid-area`
- Flying objects positioned with CSS Grid too (spanning appropriate cells)
- Use `iconOffset` as grid gap or padding

**Option 2: Hybrid Grid + Absolute (More flexible)**
- Stage uses CSS Grid 33 for icon placement
- Flying objects use position: absolute
- Use Vue refs + getBoundingClientRect() to get icon positions
- onMounted, calculate positions and update reactive state

Option 1 is cleaner but flying objects in grid cells is awkward. Option 2 is better because:
- Icons benefit from grid (auto-positioning)
- Flying objects need absolute positioning anyway (to animate freely)
- Getting real positions via refs is more accurate than calculations

Let me recommend Option 2 with specific implementation steps.

 Implementation steps for hybrid Grid + Absolute approach:

**Step 1: Update UnifiedPostsStage.vue**
- Replace position: relative with CSS Grid
- Grid template: `auto 1fr auto / auto 1fr auto`
- Add padding/gap for iconOffset spacing
- Place 4 AnimatedIcon components in corner cells using `grid-area`
- Place UnifiedGrid in center cell (2,2)

**Step 2: Update AnimatedIcon placement**
- Wrap each icon in a div with `grid-area` style
- top-left: `grid-area: 1 / 1`
- top-right: `grid-area: 1 / 3`  
- bottom-left: `grid-area: 3 / 1`
- bottom-right: `grid-area: 3 / 3`
- Center grid: `grid-area: 2 / 2`

**Step 3: Flying objects positioning**
- Keep as position: absolute (outside grid flow)
- Add template refs to icon wrapper divs
- onMounted: Use getBoundingClientRect() to get icon centers
- Create reactive state for icon positions
- Pass real positions to FlyingObject components

  Thought 7/8 

 Actually, there's an even simpler approach that avoids JavaScript positioning entirely:

**Pure CSS Grid Solution:**
- Stage: CSS Grid 33
- Icons in corner cells (1,1), (1,3), (3,1), (3,3)
- UnifiedGrid in center cell (2,2)
- Flying objects: Also placed in the SAME cells as their icons
- Use z-index to layer them above icons
- Animate from their grid cell position toward center using CSS transforms

This is cleanest because:
- No JavaScript position calculations
- No getBoundingClientRect() needed
- Fully responsive automatically
- Icons and their flying objects share the same grid cell (natural grouping)

The FlyingPostFromIcon component would:
- Be placed in the appropriate grid cell
- Contain both the AnimatedIcon AND the FlyingObjects
- Flying objects use CSS transforms to animate toward center
- All positioning handled by grid automatically

  Thought 8/8 

 Final recommendation: Pure CSS Grid 33 layout

**Architecture:**
```
UnifiedPostsStage (Grid 33)
 FlyingPostFromIcon [grid-area: 1/1] (top-left)
 FlyingPostFromIcon [grid-area: 1/3] (top-right)  
 FlyingPostFromIcon [grid-area: 3/1] (bottom-left)
 FlyingPostFromIcon [grid-area: 3/3] (bottom-right)
 UnifiedGrid [grid-area: 2/2] (center)
```

**Benefits:**
 No manual position calculations
 Icons perfectly aligned in corners
 Center grid perfectly centered
 Responsive automatic
 Simple CSS, minimal JavaScript
 Flying objects positioned relative to their grid cell
 iconOffset becomes grid gap/padding

**Changes needed:**
1. UnifiedPostsStage: Add CSS Grid with 33 layout
2. FlyingPostFromIcon: Add grid-area styling
3. Remove all manual position calculation props (stageWidth, stageHeight, iconOffset for positioning)
4. Flying objects calculate center-relative positions using CSS transforms

This is the cleanest solution.

[DEBUG] MCP server "sequential-thinking": Calling MCP tool: sequentialthinking
[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 1/5 

 Analyzing why the grid is still right of center with `1fr auto 1fr` layout:

The problem: Even with equal `1fr` side columns, the center is shifted right.

Potential causes:
1. The `1fr` columns are calculated AFTER the `auto` column takes its space
2. The icons in corner zones might be affecting column widths differently
3. The gap might be applying unevenly
4. Grid items in different rows of the same column might create unequal column widths
5. The `width: 100%` on zones might be causing issues

Key insight: CSS Grid calculates column widths based on ALL content in that column across all rows. Since row 1 has icons in columns 1 & 3, and row 3 also has icons in columns 1 & 3, but the icons might render with slightly different widths due to padding/sizing, this could create asymmetry.

Solution approaches:
1. Use `minmax(0, 1fr)` to force equal widths regardless of content
2. Remove `width: 100%` from zones to let them size naturally
3. Make center zone span full width with positioning
4. Use different grid template entirely

[DEBUG] MCP server "sequential-thinking": Calling MCP tool: sequentialthinking
[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 2/5 

 The core issue: CSS Grid's `1fr` still respects content size constraints. Even with `1fr auto 1fr`, if column 1 has different content than column 3 (different icon sizes, padding, etc.), the `1fr` units won't be truly equal.

Best solution: `minmax(0, 1fr)` forces grid to:
1. Ignore content size (the `0` minimum)
2. Distribute remaining space equally (the `1fr`)
3. Allow content to shrink/overflow if needed

This is the standard pattern for forcing equal-width grid columns regardless of content.

Alternative approach if that doesn't work: Make the center column `auto` but the center zone itself use absolute positioning to center within the stage, independent of grid calculations.

[DEBUG] MCP server "sequential-thinking": Calling MCP tool: sequentialthinking
[ERROR] MCP server "sequential-thinking" Server stderr: 
  Thought 3/5 

 Implementation plan:

Change grid columns from `'1fr auto 1fr'` to `'minmax(0, 1fr) auto minmax(0, 1fr)'`

The `minmax(0, 1fr)` pattern:
- `0` = minimum size is 0 (ignore content size completely)
- `1fr` = take 1 fractional unit of available space
- Result: Forces truly equal columns regardless of content

Also should check the zone styles - the `width: 100%` on zones might be stretching content and affecting grid calculations. Should remove or adjust zone sizing.

Additionally, the center zone might need `justify-self: center` to ensure it's centered within its grid cell.
